<div id="review_3592422544" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3592422544" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4934590-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425387897p2/4934590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3592422544?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/4934590-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3592422544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15732039359327622539">On the surface the Galvins were the picture perfect family. Mimi comes from upper-crust Texan wealth while Don, soon to become an Air Force Academy official, exudes confidence. They will grow their family until it encompassed 10 boys and 2 girls. But turmoil is a constant companion to the family. Six of the boys would eventually be diagnosed with schizophrenia bringing chaos, abuse, murder and lots of denial to the family. Honestly I'm still not sure whether Mimi Galvin was an absolute narcissis</span>
  <span id="freeText15732039359327622539" style="display:none">On the surface the Galvins were the picture perfect family. Mimi comes from upper-crust Texan wealth while Don, soon to become an Air Force Academy official, exudes confidence. They will grow their family until it encompassed 10 boys and 2 girls. But turmoil is a constant companion to the family. Six of the boys would eventually be diagnosed with schizophrenia bringing chaos, abuse, murder and lots of denial to the family. Honestly I'm still not sure whether Mimi Galvin was an absolute narcissistic monster or a tireless crusader hell bent on keeping the family together. It's a testament to Kolker's empathy that he can write this story where both are possible. <br /><br />This is also a medical mystery - following the varied research and theories over the years. It's heartbreaking to see how advances are stymied by a lack of clear profit to be made. And to see how, even decades later, the illness still proves difficult to define. <br /><br />For all the madness on display, the endless tragedies and erosion of normalcy, Kolker manages to pull hope from the mess, bookending the story with how the youngest takes on her mother's mantle and works to keep the family together. Years in the making, this is meticulously researched, pulling from extensive interviews with the entire family and the researchers looking to uncover the mysteries of this ill-understood disease. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15732039359327622539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3389196936" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3389196936" />
    <a title="Sonja Arlow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6449756-sonja-arlow"><img alt="Sonja Arlow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576564309p2/6449756.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3389196936?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sonja Arlow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sonja Arlow" href="/user/show/6449756-sonja-arlow">Sonja Arlow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/49679332-hidden-valley-road">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=medicine">medicine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=bookclub-read">bookclub-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3389196936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14993261382092962924">Imagine having 12 children! Now imagine that 6 of them are diagnosed with one of the most misunderstood illnesses of our time. Schizophrenia.<br/><br/>Even today, in a world where no subject (or body part) is taboo anymore, mental illness is still seen as a weakness to be hidden away.<br/><br/>This was a fascinating look at not only one family’s struggle with this disease but also the broader medical community and how research has developed through the decades to try and understand schizophrenia better.<br/><br/>Let’s be hon</span>
  <span id="freeText14993261382092962924" style="display:none">Imagine having 12 children! Now imagine that 6 of them are diagnosed with one of the most misunderstood illnesses of our time. Schizophrenia.<br /><br />Even today, in a world where no subject (or body part) is taboo anymore, mental illness is still seen as a weakness to be hidden away.<br /><br />This was a fascinating look at not only one family’s struggle with this disease but also the broader medical community and how research has developed through the decades to try and understand schizophrenia better.<br /><br />Let’s be honest the 1950’s to 1970’s was not the best of times for anyone with a metal illness. Lobotomies and electroshock treatment just became the fashion and patients were treated in the most horrid ways.<br /><br />The cure is sometimes more destructive than the disease.<br /><br />And the book reminded me just how much of an uphill battle medical research faces on a good day. <br /><br />The pharmaceutical industry has a "if it makes no profit we will make no pills" attitude which did not come as a surprise to me but made for frustrating reading (see nicotine &amp; nutrition studies).<br /><br />I loved how the author also made the story personal, focusing on each family member, showing how the children without mental health issues suffered just as much as their siblings in a household that descended into more and more chaos as the years progressed.<br /><br />A gripping true life story that read like fiction. Recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14993261382092962924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3315975398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3315975398" />
    <a title="Diane Yannick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1253673-diane-yannick"><img alt="Diane Yannick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468376907p2/1253673.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3315975398?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane Yannick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane Yannick" href="/user/show/1253673-diane-yannick">Diane Yannick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3315975398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4533510108188970240">Mimi Galvin had twelve children and six of them had schizophrenia. Think about that sentence for a minute. I know about Catholic's stance on birth control, but twelve is a boatload. It appeared to me that Mimi was trying to fill an insatiable hole in her own life. I could not forgive her for creating a tribe that she didn't have the skills to rear. She seemed to lose respect for her husband once he lost his status due to health problems. She seemed to favor certain children to the detriment of o</span>
  <span id="freeText4533510108188970240" style="display:none">Mimi Galvin had twelve children and six of them had schizophrenia. Think about that sentence for a minute. I know about Catholic's stance on birth control, but twelve is a boatload. It appeared to me that Mimi was trying to fill an insatiable hole in her own life. I could not forgive her for creating a tribe that she didn't have the skills to rear. She seemed to lose respect for her husband once he lost his status due to health problems. She seemed to favor certain children to the detriment of others. She perpetuated this persona of doting mother, marching them into church like ducklings. At home she was overwhelmed and distant, often playing one child against another. As the sick ones became sicker she made it her mission to make sure they got to their appointments and had their meds. What she did not do was make sure about was that there was a long term plan that avoided ping-ponging them between home and institutions. Her two girls, Margaret and Mary, suffered abuse that went unrecognized and later unheard. <br /><br />Kolker, the author, was only able to interview a few of the siblings for this book. Thus there were many brothers who were not at all fleshed out. He chose to mix the family saga with extremely detailed info about schizophrenia research. The scientific debate between nature vs nurture was informative but many of the case studies seemed redundant. For me, the brain research was interesting. Yet, we still don't have many answers today.<br /><br />So, I slogged through this book. Although many readers could, I was not able to connect to this book in any truly meaningful way. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4533510108188970240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3270576429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3270576429" />
    <a title="Tania" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6450088-tania"><img alt="Tania" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603638299p2/6450088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3270576429?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tania" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tania" href="/user/show/6450088-tania">Tania</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6450088-tania?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6450088-tania?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3270576429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5916386677965728236"><blockquote>"...schizophrenia affects an estimated one in a hundred people..."</blockquote><br/><blockquote>"One out of every twenty cases of schizophrenia ends in suicide."</blockquote><br/>3.5 stars. Shocking stats for a disease no-one really understands. In Hidden Valley Road the author introduces us to the Galvin's - an American family with twelve children, six of them diagnosed with schizophrenia. He spends many hours interviewing everyone in the family, which helps us appreciate that this illness had as much of an impact on the unafflicted children</span>
  <span id="freeText5916386677965728236" style="display:none"><blockquote>"...schizophrenia affects an estimated one in a hundred people..."</blockquote><br /><blockquote>"One out of every twenty cases of schizophrenia ends in suicide."</blockquote><br />3.5 stars. Shocking stats for a disease no-one really understands. In Hidden Valley Road the author introduces us to the Galvin's - an American family with twelve children, six of them diagnosed with schizophrenia. He spends many hours interviewing everyone in the family, which helps us appreciate that this illness had as much of an impact on the unafflicted children as on the ones having to undergo all the treatments, without any hope of being cured.<br /><br />He balances this personal account of how the disease affect a family with an in-depth look of the research done as well as the psychiatric, chemical, and biological theories through the decades. I found this very interesting, especially the contribution the Galvin family made. We are so lucky that we live in a time where there is a better understanding of psychiatric illnesses, even though there is not much of an improvement in the treatment of schizophrenia specifically.<br /><br />Well-written and empathetic<br /><br /><blockquote>"Progress comes gradually, often painfully, in fits and starts..."</blockquote> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5916386677965728236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1915054918857590139">I think my expectations were too high for this book. The book is about schizophrenia generally and its genetic components and the ongoing research into heritability, but it's more about the family with 12 kids--the majority of whom had it. I did learn somewhat more than I already knew about the disease, but not much more (read the Gene for better info) and the story of the family was too journalistic and removed to be invested in. I usually always prefer nonfiction, but I think this one might ha</span>
  <span id="freeText1915054918857590139" style="display:none">I think my expectations were too high for this book. The book is about schizophrenia generally and its genetic components and the ongoing research into heritability, but it's more about the family with 12 kids--the majority of whom had it. I did learn somewhat more than I already knew about the disease, but not much more (read the Gene for better info) and the story of the family was too journalistic and removed to be invested in. I usually always prefer nonfiction, but I think this one might have been better as a novel because the characters needed some more color to be real. <br /><br />Also, the author points out how schizophrenia was falsely blamed on bad mothers for so long--but then he kind of talks mostly about the mother (and not the father). He doesn't blame her for the disease, but he seems to put her parenting under a microscope (at least compared to the lack of much info at all about the father)</span>

<div id="review_3387482266" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3387482266" />
    <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens"><img alt="DeB MaRtEnS" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593294620p2/9827967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3387482266?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DeB MaRtEnS" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens">DeB MaRtEnS</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=biography-memoir">biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=psychology-medical">psychology-medical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=2020-year">2020-year</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3387482266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer297346366266449195">I found Hidden Valley Road all over the map. The cover- Don and Mimi Gavin standing atop a spiral staircase smiling, beaming above the arc of ten children in suits, caught my eye. It is sensational- and that six of those sons developed schizophrenia was a tragedy of Shakespearean proportions. However, I felt vaguely heartsick reading this biography- as though I was prying into a story that I had no business sticking my nose into. <br/><br/>Mimi Gavin went on to have 12 children, breeding until she put her</span>
  <span id="freeText297346366266449195" style="display:none">I found Hidden Valley Road all over the map. The cover- Don and Mimi Gavin standing atop a spiral staircase smiling, beaming above the arc of ten children in suits, caught my eye. It is sensational- and that six of those sons developed schizophrenia was a tragedy of Shakespearean proportions. However, I felt vaguely heartsick reading this biography- as though I was prying into a story that I had no business sticking my nose into. <br /><br />Mimi Gavin went on to have 12 children, breeding until she put her life in peril while her husband Don was frequently away as a military professional. As parents they lacked insight, even prior to schizophrenia developing in the eldest, and denial continued to endanger all of their children. The psychology of the times blamed the mother, until Freud lost prominence- but the pendulum has swung, of course. Genes and the environment are under current consideration - and the Gavin family helped with this course of the science, in genetic studies.<br /><br />Other families with large sibling groups do have schizophrenia and contributed to studies, but none were quite as sensational that they would be written about, apparently. This family’s dysfunction, neglect and abuse in its many forms are a challenge to consider, aside from the effects of the disease on six individuals in one family. <br /><br />I found there to be quite a bit of repetition regarding the life quandaries of the adult children, in the latter chapters of the book, as well as the information about schizophrenia, which became rather ponderous as a result. <br /><br />Some strides in the science are promising, for which the contributions of the Gavins created some hope in this otherwise very bleak biography. <br /><br />For those who have little understanding of schizophrenia, perhaps they will find this biography well framed around the Gavin family. For me, it wobbled between sensationalism, over- telling and moments of hope, which did redeem it to being readable. <br /><br />Three stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="297346366266449195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2284640-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589758860p2/2284640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3090219342?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3090219342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12906650387346662093">I mainly wanted to read this book because my mom was bipolar. She was diagnosed when I was 14 and she was 40. This book is about a family with several siblings who were diagnosed as schizophrenic. All the members of the family (14 in all if you include the parents) either had or have serious mental issues or grew up surrounded by people who did. And the one positive thing is that the family became involved in a few different research studies on whether schizophrenia is inherited, how it develops</span>
  <span id="freeText12906650387346662093" style="display:none">I mainly wanted to read this book because my mom was bipolar. She was diagnosed when I was 14 and she was 40. This book is about a family with several siblings who were diagnosed as schizophrenic. All the members of the family (14 in all if you include the parents) either had or have serious mental issues or grew up surrounded by people who did. And the one positive thing is that the family became involved in a few different research studies on whether schizophrenia is inherited, how it develops, and how it can be treated.<br /><br />Although this book was difficult for me to read at times, and it took me a little while to finish, I found it fascinating and extremely informative. And also somewhat cathartic for me as my mother passed away recently. I related to so many of the issues that the healthier siblings had to deal with and also the complicated family dynamics. In a lot of ways my mother was fortunate in that her condition was for the most part under control when she stayed on her meds (which luckily she did most of the time). <br /><br />I recommend this book, especially if you are interested in mental health issues. It’s extremely well written. Thank you to Net Galley for providing me with a copy of the book in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12906650387346662093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1329479056547781201">To be a staff pick upon publication.<br/><br/>A fascinating look into both an extraordinary family and the history of psychology and its treatment of mental illness in general and schizophrenia, in particular. The Galvin family had twelve children (following their Church’s traditions and dictates) between 1945 and 1965. Of those twelve, six of the boys developed schizophrenia and were treated (some mistreated) over decades. During that same period and into the 2000s some remarkable advancements have been </span>
  <span id="freeText1329479056547781201" style="display:none">To be a staff pick upon publication.<br /><br />A fascinating look into both an extraordinary family and the history of psychology and its treatment of mental illness in general and schizophrenia, in particular. The Galvin family had twelve children (following their Church’s traditions and dictates) between 1945 and 1965. Of those twelve, six of the boys developed schizophrenia and were treated (some mistreated) over decades. During that same period and into the 2000s some remarkable advancements have been made in how schizophrenia is viewed, why it originates (genetics mostly), and how it is treated. This book will interest any who are interested in medical history and who can stand the raw pain and devastation of a family living through constant illness, violence, sexual abuse, and more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1329479056547781201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_41552709'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41552709-the-uninhabitable-earth"><img alt="The Uninhabitable Earth: Life After Warming" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1603323079l/41552709._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/URx1pmDG9UHMvqEqpFz1CagaS0eszl0xMAT545r7HMgFnA5WwmQNIMEk/WnH0MNgU5JGS9AXZ1UaJ8QvhI7Yw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g/uWU/HN+FbHz8UMmIiZu9/cMPV6eekgTE77k0tOokNeqZe8M0dzt0P5rH2VBqlieDIQwUuKjcnc5ndkezd1Uw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

She tracks the misogyny and propaganda hidden (or not so hidden) in the media she and her peers devoured growing up, a buffet of distortions, delusions, prejudice, and outright bullsh*t that has allowed white male mediocrity to maintain a death grip on American culture and politics-and that delivered us to this precarious, disorienting moment in history.\n\nWest writes, “We were just a hair’s breadth from electing America’s first female president to succeed America’s first black president. The truth can transform us; there is witchcraft in it. The highway is known as the \'Highway of Tears\', and it has come to symbolize a national crisis.\n\nJournalist, Jessica McDiarmid, investigates the devastating effect these tragedies have had on the families of the victims and their communities, and how systemic racism and indifference have created a climate where Indigenous women are over-policed, yet under-protected. Through interviews with those closest to the victims--mothers and fathers, siblings and friends--McDiarmid offers an intimate, first-hand account of their loss and relentless fight for justice. Examining the historically fraught social and cultural tensions between settlers and Indigenous peoples in the region, McDiarmid links these cases to others across Canada--now estimated to number up to 4,000--contextualizing them within a broader examination of the undervaluing of Indigenous lives in this country.\n\nHighway of Tears is a powerful story about our ongoing failure to provide last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
